<p>The <b>Wikimedia Foundation, Inc.</b> (<b>WMF</b>, or simply <b>Wikimedia</b>) is an American non-profit and <a href="/wiki/Charitable_organization" title="Charitable organization">charitable organization</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hanson2016_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hanson2016-6">[6]</a></sup> It is mostly known for participating in the <a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_movement" title="Wikimedia movement">Wikimedia movement</a>. It owns the internet domain names of most movement projects and hosts sites like <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Foundation_(nonprofit)" title="Foundation (nonprofit)">foundation</a> was founded in 2003 by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wales" title="Jimmy Wales">Jimmy Wales</a> as a way to fund Wikipedia and its sister projects through non-profit means.<sup id="cite_ref-Rupert_Neate_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rupert_Neate-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Announcing_Wikimedia_Foundation_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Announcing_Wikimedia_Foundation-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the foundation employs over 280 people, with annual revenues in excess of <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>75 million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-2014-2015_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014-2015-9">[9]</a></sup> Christophe Henner is <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chair</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_trustees" class="mw-redirect" title="Board of trustees">board</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IrishExaminer2016_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IrishExaminer2016-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Maher" title="Katherine Maher">Katherine Maher</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Executive_director" title="Executive director">executive director</a> since March 2016.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Goal">Goal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Goal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Wikimedia Foundation has stated its goal is to develop and maintain <a href="/wiki/Open_content" title="Open content">open content</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wiki</a>-based projects and to provide the full contents of those projects to the public <a href="/wiki/Free_of_charge" class="mw-redirect" title="Free of charge">free of charge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wikimedia-mission_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wikimedia-mission-11">[11]</a></sup> Another main objective of the Wikimedia Foundation is <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_group" title="Advocacy group">political advocacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Wikimedia Foundation was granted section <a href="/wiki/501(c)(3)" class="mw-redirect" title="501(c)(3)">501(c)(3)</a> status by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Code" title="Internal Revenue Code">Internal Revenue Code</a> as a public charity in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/National_Taxonomy_of_Exempt_Entities" title="National Taxonomy of Exempt Entities">National Taxonomy of Exempt Entities</a> (NTEE) code is B60 (<a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">Adult</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continuing_education" title="Continuing education">Continuing education</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The foundation's <a href="/wiki/By-law" title="By-law">by-laws</a> declare a statement of purpose of collecting and developing educational content and to disseminate it effectively and globally.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Wikipedia" title="History of Wikipedia">History of Wikipedia</a></div>
<p>In 2001, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wales" title="Jimmy Wales">Jimmy Wales</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Internet_entrepreneur" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet entrepreneur">Internet entrepreneur</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Sanger" title="Larry Sanger">Larry Sanger</a>, an online community organizer and <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a> professor, founded Wikipedia as an Internet encyclopedia to supplement <a href="/wiki/Nupedia" title="Nupedia">Nupedia</a>. The project was originally funded by <a href="/wiki/Bomis" title="Bomis">Bomis</a>, Wales' for-profit business. As Wikipedia's popularity skyrocketed, revenues to fund the project stalled.<sup id="cite_ref-Rupert_Neate_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rupert_Neate-7">[7]</a></sup> Since Wikipedia was depleting Bomis' resources, Wales and <a href="/wiki/Larry_Sanger" title="Larry Sanger">Sanger</a> thought of a charity model to fund the project.<sup id="cite_ref-Rupert_Neate_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rupert_Neate-7">[7]</a></sup> The Wikimedia Foundation was incorporated in Florida on June 20, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Announcing_Wikimedia_Foundation_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Announcing_Wikimedia_Foundation-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It applied to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> to trademark <i>Wikipedia</i> on September 14, 2004. The mark was granted registration status on January 10, 2006. Trademark protection was accorded by Japan on December 16, 2004, and, in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, on January 20, 2005. There were plans to license the use of the Wikipedia trademark for some products, such as books or DVDs.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The name "Wikimedia", a <a href="/wiki/Compound_(linguistics)" title="Compound (linguistics)">compound</a> of <a href="/wiki/Wiki" title="Wiki">wiki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_(communication)" title="Media (communication)">media</a>, was coined by American author <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Rampton" title="Sheldon Rampton">Sheldon Rampton</a> in a post to the English mailing list in March 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> three months after <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary" title="Wiktionary">Wiktionary</a> became the second wiki-based project hosted on Wales' platform.</p>
<p>In April 2005, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">Internal Revenue Service</a> approved the foundation as an educational foundation in the category "<a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">Adult</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continuing_education" title="Continuing education">Continuing education</a>", meaning all contributions to the foundation are <a href="/wiki/Tax_deduction" title="Tax deduction">tax-deductible</a> for U.S. federal income tax purposes.</p>
<p>On December 11, 2006, the Foundation's board noted that the corporation could not become the <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">membership organization</a> initially planned but never implemented due to an inability to meet the registration requirements of Florida statutory law. Accordingly,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (February 2017)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> the by-laws were amended to remove all reference to membership rights and activities. The decision to change the bylaws was passed by the board unanimously.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 25, 2007, the foundation's board gave notice that the operations would be moving to the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a>. Major considerations cited for choosing San Francisco were proximity to like-minded organizations and potential partners, a better talent pool, as well as cheaper and more convenient international travel than is available from <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MoncadaWikimoveTribune_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoncadaWikimoveTribune-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MullinsWikimoveTribune_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MullinsWikimoveTribune-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KimWikimoveSFChronicle_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KimWikimoveSFChronicle-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lila_Tretikov" title="Lila Tretikov">Lila Tretikov</a> was appointed executive director of the Wikimedia Foundation in May 2014. She resigned in March 2016. Former chief communications officer <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Maher" title="Katherine Maher">Katherine Maher</a> was appointed the interim executive director, a position made permanent in June 2016.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Projects_and_initiatives">Projects and initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Projects and initiatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wikimedia_projects"><span id="Projects"></span> Wikimedia projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Wikimedia projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the complete list, see <a href="https://wikimediafoundation.org/wiki/Special:SiteMatrix" class="extiw" title="foundation:Special:SiteMatrix">foundation:Special:SiteMatrix</a> and <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Complete_list_of_Wikimedia_projects" class="extiw" title="m:Complete list of Wikimedia projects">m:Complete list of Wikimedia projects</a>.</div>
<p>Content on most Wikimedia Foundation <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">websites</a> is licensed for redistribution under <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Text_of_Creative_Commons_Attribution-ShareAlike_3.0_Unported_License" title="Wikipedia:Text of Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported License">v3.0</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Attribution_(copyright)" title="Attribution (copyright)">Attribution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Share-alike" title="Share-alike">Share-alike</a> <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons_license" title="Creative Commons license">Creative Commons licenses</a>. This content is sourced from contributing volunteers and from resources with few or no <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">copyright</a> restrictions, such as <a href="/wiki/Copyleft" title="Copyleft">copyleft</a> material and works in the <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">public domain</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_projects">Content projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Content projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In addition to Wikipedia, the foundation operates ten other wikis that follow the <a href="/wiki/Free_content" title="Free content">free content</a> model with their main goal being the dissemination of knowledge. These include, by launch date:</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_and_coordination_projects">Infrastructure and coordination projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Infrastructure and coordination projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several additional projects exist to provide infrastructure or coordination of the free knowledge projects. For instance, <a href="https://outreach.wikimedia.org/wiki/" class="extiw" title="outreach:">Outreach</a> gives guidelines for best practices on encouraging the use of Wikimedia sites. These include:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Movement_affiliates">Movement affiliates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Movement affiliates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_movement" title="Wikimedia movement">Wikimedia movement</a></div>
<p>Wikimedia movement affiliates are independent, but formally recognized, groups of people intended to work together to support and contribute to the Wikimedia movement. The Wikimedia Foundation's Board of Trustees has approved three active models for movement affiliates: chapters, thematic organizations, and user groups. Movement affiliates are intended to organize and engage in activities to support and contribute to the Wikimedia movement, such as regional conferences, outreach, <a href="/wiki/Edit-a-thon" title="Edit-a-thon">edit-a-thons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hackathon" title="Hackathon">hackathons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_relation" class="mw-redirect" title="Public relation">public relations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_policy" title="Public policy">public policy</a> advocacy, <a href="/wiki/GLAM_(industry_sector)" title="GLAM (industry sector)">GLAM</a> engagement, and <a href="/wiki/Wikimania" title="Wikimania">Wikimania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma-faq_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-faq-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma-models_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-models-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recognition of a chapter and thematic organization is approved by the foundation's board. Recommendations on recognition of chapters and thematic organizations are made to the foundation's board by an <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Affiliations_Committee" class="extiw" title="m:Affiliations Committee">Affiliations Committee</a>, composed of Wikimedia community volunteers. The Affiliations Committee approves the recognition of individual user groups. While movement affiliates are formally recognized by the Wikimedia Foundation, they are independent of the Wikimedia Foundation, with no legal control of nor responsibility for the Wikimedia projects.<sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma-faq_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-faq-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma-models_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-models-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meta-affcom_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-affcom-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The foundation began recognizing chapters in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-MetaChap_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetaChap-36">[36]</a></sup> In 2010, development on additional models began. In 2012, the foundation approved, finalized, and adopted the thematic organization and user group recognition models. An additional model, movement partners, was also approved but as of 27 October 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> has not yet been finalized or adopted.<sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-meta-wma-models_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meta-wma-models-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wmf-wma-resolution_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wmf-wma-resolution-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wikimania">Wikimania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Wikimania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wikimania" title="Wikimania">Wikimania</a></div>
<p>Each year, an international conference called Wikimania brings the people together who are involved in the Wikimedia organizations and projects. The first Wikimania was held in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, Germany, in 2005. Nowadays, Wikimania is organized by a committee supported usually by the national chapter, in collaboration with the Wikimedia Foundation. Wikimania has been held in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2009-website_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009-website-38">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cambridge,_Massachusetts" title="Cambridge, Massachusetts">Cambridge</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-attendees2006_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-attendees2006-39">[39]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Haifa" title="Haifa">Haifa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-themarker_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-themarker-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2015, Wikimania took place in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In 2016, Wikimania was held in <a href="/wiki/Esino_Lario" title="Esino Lario">Esino Lario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategic_plan">Strategic plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Strategic plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Katherine_Maher.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Katherine_Maher.jpg/220px-Katherine_Maher.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Katherine_Maher.jpg/330px-Katherine_Maher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Katherine_Maher.jpg/440px-Katherine_Maher.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5430" data-file-height="3620" /></a>

Executive director <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Maher" title="Katherine Maher">Katherine Maher</a>, 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In response to the growing size and popularity of Wikipedia, the Wikimedia Foundation announced a Strategic Plan to improve and sustain the Wikimedia movement. The plan was announced in July 2009, followed by a process of interviews and surveys with people from across the Wikimedia movement, including board of trustees, members of staff and volunteer editors.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The ongoing plan was intended to be the basis of a five-year plan to further outreach, improve content quality and quality control, and optimising operational areas such as finance and infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wikipedia_Usability_Initiative">Wikipedia Usability Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Wikipedia Usability Initiative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2008, the Wikimedia Foundation announced a restricted donation grant of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$890,000</span> from the <a href="/wiki/Stanton_Foundation" title="Stanton Foundation">Stanton Foundation</a>, to improve Wikipedia's accessibility.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Later named the Wikipedia Usability Initiative, the grant was used by the Wikimedia Foundation to appoint project-specific staff to the technology department.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>A series of surveys were conducted throughout 2009. This began with a qualitative environment survey on <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">MediaWiki</a> extensions, followed by a Qualitative Statistical Survey focusing on volume of edits, number of new users, and related statistics. In March 2009, a usability and experience study was carried out on new and non-editors of the English Wikipedia. The aim was to discover what obstacles participants encountered while editing Wikipedia, ranging from small changes to more complicated syntax such as templates. The study recruited 2500 people for in-person laboratory testing via the Wikipedia website, which was filtered down to ten participants. The results were collated and used by the technology team to improve Wikipedia's usability.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The Usability and Experience Study was followed up by the Usability, Experience and Progress Study in September 2009. This study recruited different new and non-editors for in-person trials on a new Wikipedia skin.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The initiative ultimately culminated in a new Wikipedia skin named Vector, constructed based on the results of the usability studies. This was introduced by default in stages, beginning in May 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Policy_Initiative">Public Policy Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Public Policy Initiative">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2010, the Wikimedia Foundation announced the Public Policy Initiative, following a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.2 million</span> donation by the Stanton Foundation. The Initiative was set up to improve articles relating to public policy–related issues.<sup id="cite_ref-pubpol_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pubpol-52">[52]</a></sup> As part of the initiative, Wikipedia collaborated with ten universities to help students and professors create and maintain articles relating to public policy.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Volunteer editors of Wikipedia, known as "ambassadors", provided assistance to students and professors. This was either done on campus sites or online.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2017, the Foundation was one of the founding partners in the <a href="/wiki/Initiative_for_Open_Citations" title="Initiative for Open Citations">Initiative for Open Citations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-I4OC_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I4OC-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The foundation employs technology including hardware and software to run its projects.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware">Hardware</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hardware">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia#Hardware_operations_and_support" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia §&#160;Hardware operations and support</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png/220px-Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png/330px-Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png/440px-Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png 2x" data-file-width="1303" data-file-height="1672" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikipedia_webrequest_flow_2015-10.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Overview of system architecture, October 2015. See <a href="https://meta.wikimedia.org/wiki/Server_layout_diagrams" class="extiw" title="meta:Server layout diagrams">server layout diagrams on Meta-Wiki</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg/220px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg/330px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg/440px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="2206" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_Servers-8055_13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wikimedia Foundation servers</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Wikipedia employed a single server until 2004, when the server setup was expanded into a distributed <a href="/wiki/Multitier_architecture" title="Multitier architecture">multitier architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2005, the project ran on 39 <a href="/wiki/Dedicated_hosting_service" title="Dedicated hosting service">dedicated servers</a> in Florida.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This configuration included a single master <a href="/wiki/Database_server" title="Database server">database server</a> running <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a>, multiple database servers, 21 <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">web servers</a> running the <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">Apache HTTP Server</a>, and seven <a href="/wiki/Squid_(software)" title="Squid (software)">Squid cache</a> servers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Wikimedia currently runs on dedicated <a href="/wiki/Cluster_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cluster (computing)">clusters</a> of <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> servers (mainly <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">Ubuntu</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> As of December 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 300 in Florida and 44 in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-servers_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-servers-59">[59]</a></sup> The number of servers needed to run the infrastructure has been mostly stable since then: 520 servers are used in the main cluster (eqiad) as of November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2015, the system still runs on central master database and application servers, but there are several <a href="/wiki/Cache_(computing)" title="Cache (computing)">cache layers</a> with various ever-changing technologies, as well as a multitude of subsystems for DNS resolution, load balancing, metrics, monitoring, other system administration etc.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Softwаrе"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Softw.D0.B0r.D0.B5">Softwаrе</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Softwаrе">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The operation of Wikimedia depends on <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">MediaWiki</a>, a custom-made, <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free</a> and <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source</a> <a href="/wiki/Wiki_software" title="Wiki software">wiki software</a> platform written in <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a> and built upon the <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> database.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The software incorporates programming features such as a <a href="/wiki/Macro_(computer_science)" title="Macro (computer science)">macro language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Variable_(programming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Variable (programming)">variables</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Transclusion" title="Transclusion">transclusion</a> system for <a href="/wiki/Web_template" class="mw-redirect" title="Web template">templates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/URL_redirection" title="URL redirection">URL redirection</a>. MediaWiki is licensed under the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU General Public License</a> and it is used by all Wikimedia projects, as well as many other wiki projects. Originally, Wikipedia ran on <a href="/wiki/UseModWiki" title="UseModWiki">UseModWiki</a> written in <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a> by Clifford Adams (Phase I), which initially required <a href="/wiki/CamelCase" class="mw-redirect" title="CamelCase">CamelCase</a> for article hyperlinks; the present double bracket style was incorporated later. Starting in January 2002 (Phase II), Wikipedia began running on a <a href="/wiki/PhpWiki" title="PhpWiki">PHP wiki</a> engine with a MySQL database; this software was custom-made for Wikipedia by <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Manske" title="Magnus Manske">Magnus Manske</a>. The Phase II software was repeatedly modified to accommodate the <a href="/wiki/Exponential_growth" title="Exponential growth">exponentially increasing</a> demand. In July 2002 (Phase III), Wikipedia shifted to the third-generation software, MediaWiki, originally written by <a href="/wiki/Lee_Daniel_Crocker" title="Lee Daniel Crocker">Lee Daniel Crocker</a>. Several MediaWiki extensions are <a href="/wiki/Special:Version#Installed_extensions" title="Special:Version">installed</a> to extend the functionality of MediaWiki software. In April 2005, a <a href="/wiki/Lucene" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucene">Lucene</a> extension<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> was added to MediaWiki's built-in search and Wikipedia switched from <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a> to Lucene for searching. Currently Lucene Search 2.1,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> which is written in <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> and based on Lucene library 2.3,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> is used. Wikimedia Foundation also uses <a href="/wiki/CiviCRM" title="CiviCRM">CiviCRM</a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/WordPress" title="WordPress">WordPress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Foundation published official Wikipedia <a href="/wiki/Mobile_apps" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile apps">mobile apps</a> for <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> devices and in March 2015, the apps were updated to include mobile user friendly features.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_general">In general</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In general">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg/220px-Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg.png" width="220" height="348" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg/330px-Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg/440px-Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="950" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_financial_development_multilanguage.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Financial development of the Wikimedia Foundation (in US$), 2003–2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Wikimedia Foundation relies on public contributions and grants to fund its mission.<sup id="cite_ref-financialstatements_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialstatements-70">[70]</a></sup> It is exempt from federal income tax<sup id="cite_ref-financialstatements_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialstatements-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and from state income tax.<sup id="cite_ref-financialstatements_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialstatements-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> It is not a private foundation, and contributions to it qualify as tax-deductible charitable contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-financialstatements_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialstatements-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>The continued technical and economic growth of each of the Wikimedia projects is dependent mostly on donations but the Wikimedia Foundation also increases its revenue by alternative means of funding such as <a href="/wiki/Federal_grant" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal grant">grants</a>, sponsorship, services and brand merchandising. The Wikimedia <a href="/wiki/OAI-PMH" class="mw-redirect" title="OAI-PMH">OAI-PMH</a> update feed service, targeted primarily at search engines and similar bulk analysis and republishing, has been a source of revenue for several years,<sup id="cite_ref-financialstatements_70-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialstatements-70">[70]</a></sup> but is no longer open to new customers.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/DBpedia" title="DBpedia">DBpedia</a> was given access to this feed free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In July 2014, the Foundation announced it would be accepting <a href="/wiki/Bitcoin" title="Bitcoin">Bitcoin</a> donations.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the end of fiscal year ended 2004, the Foundation's net assets have grown from <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$57,000</span><sup id="cite_ref-financialstatements2006_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-financialstatements2006-76">[76]</a></sup> to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$53.5 million</span> at the end of fiscal year ended June 30, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-2013-2014_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013-2014-77">[77]</a></sup> Under the leadership of Sue Gardner, who joined the Wikimedia Foundation in 2007, the Foundation's staff levels, number of donors and revenue have seen very significant growth.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Charity_Navigator" title="Charity Navigator">Charity Navigator</a> gave Wikimedia an overall rating of three out of four possible stars<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Charity Navigator gave three out of four possible stars in overall rating for fiscal years 2008 and 2009 which improved to four-stars in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> As of December 2016, the current overall rating was four stars.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grants">Grants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Grants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg/220px-Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg/330px-Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg/440px-Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1993" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Finance_Meeting_Paris_2012-02-18_n06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wikimedia Foundation and chapters finance meeting 2012, Paris</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2008, the Foundation announced a large donation, at the time its largest donation yet: a three-year, <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3 million</span> grant from the <a href="/wiki/Alfred_P._Sloan_Foundation" title="Alfred P. Sloan Foundation">Alfred P. Sloan Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3mill_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3mill-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, the Foundation received four grants&#160;– the first grant was a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$890,000</span> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Stanton_(executive)" title="Frank Stanton (executive)">Stanton Foundation</a> grant which was aimed to help study and simplify user interface for first-time authors of Wikipedia.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The second was a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$300,000</span> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">Ford Foundation</a> Grant, given in July 2009, for <a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_Commons" title="Wikimedia Commons">Wikimedia Commons</a> that aimed to improve the interfaces and workflows for multimedia uploading on Wikimedia websites.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In August 2009, the Foundation received a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500,000</span> grant from The William and Flora <a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Foundation" title="Hewlett Foundation">Hewlett Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Lastly, in August 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Omidyar_Network" title="Omidyar Network">Omidyar Network</a> issued a potential<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2 million</span> in "grant" funding to Wikimedia.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> corporation donated <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2 million</span> to the Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stanton_Foundation" title="Stanton Foundation">Stanton Foundation</a> granted $1.2 million to fund the Public Policy Initiative, a pilot program for what would later become the Wikipedia Education Program (and the spinoff <a href="/wiki/Wiki_Education_Foundation" title="Wiki Education Foundation">Wiki Education Foundation</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Also in 2010, the William and Flora Hewlett Foundation pledged a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$800,000</span> grant and all was funded during 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In March 2011, the Alfred P. Sloan Foundation authorized another <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3 million</span> grant to continue to develop and maintain the Foundation's mission. The grant was to be funded over three years with the first <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 million</span> funded in July 2011 and the remaining <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$2 million</span> was scheduled to be funded in August 2012 and 2013. In August 2011, the Stanton Foundation pledged to fund a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$3.6 million</span> grant of which <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.8 million</span> was funded and the remaining was due to be funded in September 2012. As of 2011, this was the largest grant received by the Wikimedia Foundation to-date.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In November 2011, the Foundation received a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500,000</span> donation from Google co-founder <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a> and his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-foundationgrants_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundationgrants-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, the Foundation was awarded a grant of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1.25 million</span> from the historians <a href="/wiki/Lisbet_Rausing" title="Lisbet Rausing">Lisbet Rausing</a><sup id="cite_ref-foundationgrants_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundationgrants-92">[92]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Baldwin_(professor)" title="Peter Baldwin (professor)">Peter Baldwin</a> through <a href="/wiki/Charities_Aid_Foundation" title="Charities Aid Foundation">Charities Aid Foundation</a>, scheduled to be funded in five equal installments. The first installment of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$250,000</span> was received in April 2012 and the remaining were to be funded in December 2012 through 2015. In 2014, the Foundation received the largest single gift in its history, a $5 million unrestricted donation from an anonymous donor supporting $1 million worth of expenses annually for the next five years.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, a grant agreement was reached with the <i><a href="/wiki/John_S._and_James_L._Knight_Foundation" title="John S. and James L. Knight Foundation">John S. and James L. Knight Foundation</a></i> to build a search engine called the "<a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Engine_(Wikimedia_Foundation)" title="Knowledge Engine (Wikimedia Foundation)">Knowledge Engine</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ArsKE_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArsKE-96">[96]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_Trustees">Board of Trustees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Board of Trustees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG/220px-Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG/330px-Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG/440px-Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christophe_Henner_d%C3%A9fend_son_bilan.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Christophe Henner, the current Chairman of the Board</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="https://wikimediafoundation.org/wiki/Board_of_Trustees" class="extiw" title="foundation:Board of Trustees">Board of Trustees</a> has ultimate authority of all the businesses and affairs of the Foundation. It is composed of ten members:</p>
<ul>
<li>four who are appointed by the board itself;</li>
<li>three who are selected by the community encompassed by all the different Wikimedia projects;</li>
<li>two who are selected by the local chapters and thematic organizations;</li>
<li>and one <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emeritus</a> for the foundation's founder, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wales" title="Jimmy Wales">Jimmy Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-April2008_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-April2008-105">[105]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Three permanent entities support the board on its mission and responsibilities: an executive director, who leads and oversees the operational arm of the foundation; an advisory board composed of individuals selected by the board itself that advise the board on different matters; and <a href="/wiki/Standing_committee" class="mw-redirect" title="Standing committee">standing committees</a> to which the board delegates certain matters while retaining ultimate authority. The board has also at times created other orthodox entities<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> to support itself, such as <a href="/wiki/Executive_secretary" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive secretary">executive secretaries</a> and ad-hoc committees established for specific tasks.</p>
<p>The current board comprises <a href="/w/index.php?title=Christophe_Henner&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Christophe Henner (page does not exist)">Christophe Henner</a> as chairman and María Sefidari as vice-chairman, together with Alice Wiegand, Nataliia Tymkiv, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Battles" class="mw-redirect" title="Kelly Battles">Kelly Battles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dariusz_Jemielniak" title="Dariusz Jemielniak">Dariusz Jemielniak</a> as members at-large, and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Wales" title="Jimmy Wales">Jimmy Wales</a> as <a href="/wiki/Founder%27s_seat" class="mw-redirect" title="Founder's seat">founder's seat</a> (installed as "Community Founder Trustee Position" to the WMF bylaws in August 2008).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> There are three vacant seats, most recently occupied by <a href="/wiki/Arnnon_Geshuri" title="Arnnon Geshuri">Arnnon Geshuri</a>, Denny Vrandečić and <a href="/wiki/Guy_Kawasaki" title="Guy Kawasaki">Guy Kawasaki</a>.</p>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Wikipedia_Signpost/2016-01-13/In_focus" title="Wikipedia:Wikipedia Signpost/2016-01-13/In focus">high-profile decision</a> of 2015, <a href="/wiki/James_Heilman" title="James Heilman">James Heilman</a> was removed from the board,<sup id="cite_ref-Lih2016_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lih2016-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> with little explanation.<sup id="cite_ref-Lih2016_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lih2016-108">[108]</a></sup> In January 2016, <a href="/wiki/Arnnon_Geshuri" title="Arnnon Geshuri">Arnnon Geshuri</a> stepped down from the board following a controversy about an agreement he executed when at <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, violating <a href="/wiki/United_States_antitrust_law" title="United States antitrust law">United States antitrust law</a>. The participating companies paid US$415 million in a class action suit on behalf of affected employees.<sup id="cite_ref-Mullin2016_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mullin2016-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advisory_board">Advisory board</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Advisory board">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Advisory Board, according to the Wikimedia Foundation, is an international network of experts who have agreed to give the foundation meaningful help on a regular basis in many different areas, including law, organizational development, technology, policy, and outreach.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff">Staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_appointments">First appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: First appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

<div class="thumbcaption">

Staff and workplace at Wikimedia Foundation's <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> office</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2004, the foundation appointed Tim Starling as developer liaison to help improve the <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">MediaWiki</a> software, Daniel Mayer as chief financial officer (<a href="/wiki/Management_accounting" title="Management accounting">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budgeting" class="mw-redirect" title="Budgeting">budgeting</a>, and coordination of fund drives), and <a href="/wiki/Erik_M%C3%B6ller" title="Erik Möller">Erik Möller</a> as content partnership coordinator. In May 2005, the foundation announced seven more official appointments.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2006, the foundation created several committees, including the Communication Committee, in an attempt to further organize activities essentially handled by volunteers at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Starling resigned that month to spend more time on his PhD program.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employees">Employees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Employees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg/220px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg/330px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg/440px-Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4984" data-file-height="3322" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikimedia_Foundation_Office_Officey_Photos-5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A workers area at the Wikimedia Foundation's San Francisco headquarters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The foundation's functions were, for the first few years, executed almost entirely by volunteers. In 2005, it had only two employees, Danny Wool, a coordinator, and Brion Vibber, a software manager.</p>
<p>As of October 4, 2006<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the foundation had five paid employees:<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> two programmers, an administrative assistant, a coordinator handling fundraising and grants, and an interim <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">executive director</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Brad Patrick, previously the foundation's <a href="/wiki/General_counsel" title="General counsel">general counsel</a>. Patrick ceased his activity as interim director in January 2007, and then resigned from his position as legal counsel, effective April 1, 2007. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Godwin" title="Mike Godwin">Mike Godwin</a>, who served as general counsel and legal coordinator from July 2007<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> until 2010.</p>
<p>In January 2007, Carolyn Doran was named chief operating officer and Sandy Ordonez joined as <a href="https://wikimediafoundation.org/wiki/Head_of_Communications" class="extiw" title="wmf:Head of Communications">head of communications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Doran began working as a part-time bookkeeper in 2006 after being sent by a <a href="/wiki/Temporary_work" title="Temporary work">temporary agency</a>. Doran, found to have had a long criminal record,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> left the foundation in July 2007, and <a href="/wiki/Sue_Gardner" title="Sue Gardner">Sue Gardner</a> was hired as consultant and special advisor (later CEO). Doran's departure from the organization was cited by Florence Devouard as one of the reasons the foundation took about seven months to release its fiscal 2007 financial audit.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:149_New_Montgomery_Street,_San_Francisco.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/149_New_Montgomery_Street%2C_San_Francisco.jpg/220px-149_New_Montgomery_Street%2C_San_Francisco.jpg" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/149_New_Montgomery_Street%2C_San_Francisco.jpg/330px-149_New_Montgomery_Street%2C_San_Francisco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/149_New_Montgomery_Street%2C_San_Francisco.jpg/440px-149_New_Montgomery_Street%2C_San_Francisco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1731" data-file-height="860" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:149_New_Montgomery_Street,_San_Francisco.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The location of the Wikimedia Foundation's San Francisco headquarters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Danny Wool, officially the grant coordinator but also largely involved in <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">fundraising</a> and business development, resigned in March 2007. He accused Wales of misusing the foundation's funds for recreational purposes, and said that Wales had his Wikimedia credit card taken away in part because of his spending habits, a claim Wales denied.<sup id="cite_ref-Moses_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moses-121">[121]</a></sup> In February 2007, the foundation added a new position, chapters coordinator, and hired Delphine Ménard,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> who had been occupying the position as a volunteer since August 2005. Cary Bass was hired in March 2007 in the position of volunteer coordinator. Oleta McHenry was brought in as accountant in May 2007, through a temporary placement agency and made the official full-time accountant in August 2007. In January 2008, the foundation appointed Veronique Kessler as the new chief financial and operating officer, Kul Wadhwa as head of business development, and Jay Walsh as head of communications.</p>
<p>As of June 16, 2017,<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the foundation had approximately 280 employees and contractors.<sup id="cite_ref-WMF_staff_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMF_staff-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Disputes_and_lawsuits">Disputes and lawsuits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Disputes and lawsuits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Litigation_involving_the_Wikimedia_Foundation" title="Litigation involving the Wikimedia Foundation">Litigation involving the Wikimedia Foundation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg/220px-Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg/330px-Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg/440px-Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Post-Sopa_Blackout_Party_for_Wikimedia_Foundation_staff-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wikimedia Foundation post-<a href="/wiki/Stop_Online_Piracy_Act" title="Stop Online Piracy Act">SOPA</a> party, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many disputes have resulted in <a href="/wiki/Litigation" class="mw-redirect" title="Litigation">litigation</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> while others have not.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Attorney Matt Zimmerman stated, "Without strong liability protection, it would be difficult for Wikipedia to continue to provide a platform for user-created encyclopedia content."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2011, the Foundation hired Washington, DC lobbyist <a href="/wiki/Dow_Lohnes" title="Dow Lohnes">Dow Lohnes</a> Government Strategies LLC to lobby the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> with regard to "Civil Rights/Civil Liberties" and "Copyright/Patent/Trademark."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> At the time of the hire the Foundation was concerned specifically about a bill known as the <a href="/wiki/Stop_Online_Piracy_Act" title="Stop Online Piracy Act">Stop Online Piracy Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2013, a German Court ruled that the Wikimedia Foundation can be held liable for content added to Wikipedia – however, this applies only when there has been a specific complaint; otherwise, the Wikimedia Foundation does not check any of the content published on Wikipedia and has no duty to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014, a copyright infringement lawsuit was filed by Bildkonst Upphovsrätt i Sverige against Wikimedia Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 20, 2014, a defamation lawsuit (Law Division civil case No. L-1400-14) involving Wikipedia editors was filed with the Mercer County Superior Court in New Jersey seeking, inter alia, compensatory and punitive damages.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a March 10, 2015, op-ed for <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, Wales and Tretikov announced the Foundation was filing <a href="/wiki/ACLU_and_others_v._NSA" class="mw-redirect" title="ACLU and others v. NSA">a lawsuit</a> against the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a>, calling into question its practice of <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance" title="Mass surveillance">mass surveillance</a>, which they argued infringed the constitutional rights of the Foundation's readers, editors and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rayman_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rayman-137">[137]</a></sup> On October 23, 2015, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Maryland" title="United States District Court for the District of Maryland">United States District Court for the District of Maryland</a> dismissed the suit <i><a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation_v._NSA" title="Wikimedia Foundation v. NSA">Wikimedia Foundation v. NSA</a></i> on grounds of <a href="/wiki/Standing_(law)" title="Standing (law)">standing</a>. US District Judge <a href="/wiki/T._S._Ellis_III" title="T. S. Ellis III">T. S. Ellis III</a> ruled that the plaintiffs could not plausibly prove they were subject to <a href="/wiki/Upstream_surveillance" class="mw-redirect" title="Upstream surveillance">upstream surveillance</a>, and that their argument is riddled with assumptions, speculations and mathematical gymnastics.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The plaintiffs filed an appeal with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Fourth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Fourth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Fourth Circuit</a> on February 17, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2016, Lila Tretikov announced her resignation as executive director, as a result of the WMF's controversial <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Engine_(Wikimedia_Foundation)" title="Knowledge Engine (Wikimedia Foundation)">Knowledge Engine</a> project and disagreements with the staff.<sup id="cite_ref-Hern2016_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hern2016-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel2016_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel2016-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wikimedia_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
